Basis Of Accounting Policy Policy Text Block|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|Basis of Presentation and PreparationThe condensed consolidated financial statements include the accounts of Apple Inc. and its wholly owned subsidiaries (collectively “Apple” or the “Company”). Intercompany accounts and transactions have been eliminated. In the opinion of the Company’s management, the condensed consolidated financial statements reflect all adjustments, which are normal and recurring in nature, necessary for fair financial statement presentation. The preparation of these condensed consolidated financial statements and accompanying notes in conformity with U.S. generally accepted accounting principles requires management to make estimates and assumptions that affect the amounts reported. Actual results could differ materially from those estimates. Certain prior period amounts in the condensed consolidated financial statements and accompanying notes have been reclassified to conform to the current period’s presentation. These condensed consolidated financial statements and accompanying notes should be read in conjunction with the Company’s annual consolidated financial statements and accompanying notes included in its Annual Report on Form 10-K for the fiscal year ended September 25, 2021.|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-

Fiscal Period|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|The Company’s fiscal year is the 52- or 53-week period that ends on the last Saturday of September. An additional week is included in the first fiscal quarter every five or six years to realign the Company’s fiscal quarters with calendar quarters. The Company’s fiscal years 2022 and 2021 span 52 weeks each. Unless otherwise stated, references to particular years, quarters, months and periods refer to the Company’s fiscal years ended in September and the associated quarters, months and periods of those fiscal years.|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-

  Basis Of Accounting Policy Policy Text Block|c-1|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|Basis of Presentation and PreparationThe condensed consolidated financial statements include the accounts of Apple Inc. and its wholly owned subsidiaries (collectively “Apple” or the “Company”). Intercompany accounts and transactions have been eliminated. In the opinion of the Company’s management, the condensed consolidated financial statements reflect all adjustments, which are normal and recurring in nature, necessary for fair financial statement presentation. The preparation of these condensed consolidated financial statements and accompanying notes in conformity with U.S. generally accepted accounting principles requires management to make estimates and assumptions that affect the amounts reported. Actual results could differ materially from those estimates. Certain prior period amounts in the condensed consolidated financial statements and accompanying notes have been reclassified to conform to the current period’s presentation. These condensed consolidated financial statements and accompanying notes should be read in conjunction with the Company’s annual consolidated financial statements and accompanying notes included in its Annual Report on Form 10-K for the fiscal year ended September 25, 2021.|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-
  Fiscal Period|c-1|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|The Company’s fiscal year is the 52- or 53-week period that ends on the last Saturday of September. An additional week is included in the first fiscal quarter every five or six years to realign the Company’s fiscal quarters with calendar quarters. The Company’s fiscal years 2022 and 2021 span 52 weeks each. Unless otherwise stated, references to particular years, quarters, months and periods refer to the Company’s fiscal years ended in September and the associated quarters, months and periods of those fiscal years.|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-|-

@VALUE: Basis of Presentation and PreparationThe condensed consolidated financial statements include the accounts of Apple Inc. and its wholly owned subsidiaries (collectively “Apple” or the “Company”). In the opinion of the Company’s management, the condensed consolidated financial statements reflect all adjustments, which are normal and recurring in nature, necessary for fair financial statement presentation. The preparation of these condensed consolidated financial statements and accompanying notes in conformity with U.S. generally accepted accounting principles requires management to make estimates and assumptions that affect the amounts reported. Actual results could differ materially from those estimates. Certain prior period amounts in the condensed consolidated financial statements and accompanying notes have been reclassified to conform to the current period’s presentation. - Current Assets + Non-Current Assets = Total Assets
- Current Liabilities + Non-Current Liabilities + Equity = Total Liabilities and Equity
- Gross Profit = Revenue - Cost of Revenue
- Net Income = Revenue - Expenses + Other Income/Expenses - Taxes

@TEXT_REF: The Company’s business, reputation, results of operations and financial condition, as well as the price of the Company’s stock, can be affected by a number of factors, whether currently known or unknown, including those described in Part I, Item 1A of the 2021 Form 10-K under the heading “Risk Factors.” When any one or more of these risks materialize from time to time, the Company’s business, reputation, results of operations and financial condition, as well as the price of the Company’s stock, can be materially and adversely affected. There have been no material changes to the Company’s risk factors since the 2021 Form 10-K.|tb-1

The timing of product introductions can also impact the Company’s net sales to its indirect distribution channels as these channels are filled with new inventory following a product launch, and channel inventory of an older product often declines as the launch of a newer product approaches. Net sales can also be affected when consumers and distributors anticipate a product introduction.|tb-1

@EXAMPLE_EXTRACTION
Example of how to extract and format data from this document:

```python
# Extract revenue information for specific period with hierarchy awareness
def extract_revenue(document, context_code):
    # Find the Revenue section
    revenue_section = find_section(document, '<Revenue>')

    # Extract all line items with their context codes
    revenue_data = {}
    totals = {}
    parent_child_map = {}

    # First pass: collect all items and identify parent-child relationships
    for line in revenue_section:
        if context_code in line.split('|')[1].strip():
            columns = line.split('|')
            raw_item_name = columns[0].strip()

            # Parse hierarchy information
            if raw_item_name.startswith('@TOTAL:'):
                # This is a total item
                item_name = raw_item_name.replace('@TOTAL:', '').strip()
                is_total = True
                level = 0  # Top level
            elif raw_item_name.startswith('@SUBTOTAL:'):
                # This is a subtotal item
                item_name = raw_item_name.replace('@SUBTOTAL:', '').strip()
                is_total = True
                level = 1  # Mid level
            elif '@CHILD_OF:' in raw_item_name:
                # This is a child item, extract its parent
                parts = raw_item_name.split('@CHILD_OF:')
                item_name = parts[0].replace('↳', '').strip()
                parent_name = parts[1].strip()
                parent_child_map[item_name] = parent_name
                is_total = False
                level = 2  # Child level
            else:
                # Regular item
                item_name = raw_item_name.strip()
                is_total = False
                level = 1  # Base level

            # Find the value corresponding to the context code
            value = get_value_for_context(columns, context_code)

            # Store with hierarchy information
            if is_total:
                totals[item_name] = {
                    'value': value,
                    'level': level,
                    'components': []  # Will be filled in second pass
                }
            else:
                revenue_data[item_name] = {
                    'value': value,
                    'level': level,
                    'parent': parent_child_map.get(item_name)
                }

    # Second pass: associate children with their parent totals
    for item_name, item_data in revenue_data.items():
        parent = item_data.get('parent')
        if parent and parent in totals:
            totals[parent]['components'].append(item_name)

    # Combine the data structures
    result = {
        'line_items': revenue_data,
        'totals': totals,
        # Include verification formulas
        'verify': {
            'sum_components': 'Sum of all components should equal the total',
            'formula': 'Total_Revenue = Product_Revenue + Service_Revenue + Other_Revenue'
        }
    }
    return result
```

Example hierarchical data format for extraction:

```json
{
  "line_items": {
    "Product_Revenue": {
      "value": 72480,
      "level": 1,
      "parent": "Total_Revenue"
    },
    "Service_Revenue": {
      "value": 16320,
      "level": 1,
      "parent": "Total_Revenue"
    },
    "Automotive_Revenue": {
      "value": 52300,
      "level": 2,
      "parent": "Product_Revenue"
    },
    "Energy_Revenue": {
      "value": 20180,
      "level": 2,
      "parent": "Product_Revenue"
    }
  },
  "totals": {
    "Total_Revenue": {
      "value": 88800,
      "level": 0,
      "components": ["Product_Revenue", "Service_Revenue"],
      "contexts": {
        "c-1": 88800,           // Using short code
        "FY2023": 88800,        // Using semantic code
        "Consolidated_2023": 88800  // Using segment information
      }
    },
    "Product_Revenue": {
      "value": 72480,
      "level": 1,
      "components": ["Automotive_Revenue", "Energy_Revenue"]
    }
  },
  "verify": {
    "equations": [
      "Total_Revenue = Product_Revenue + Service_Revenue",
      "Product_Revenue = Automotive_Revenue + Energy_Revenue"
    ],
    "verified": true
  },
  "metadata": {
    "statement_type": "Income_Statement",
    "period": "FY2023",
    "hierarchical": true
  }
}
```

Note: This hierarchical structure makes parent-child relationships explicit, enabling accurate calculation and validation of totals. The hierarchy levels indicate:
- Level 0: Main totals (like Total Revenue)
- Level 1: Major categories (like Product Revenue)
- Level 2: Subcategories (like Automotive Revenue)

You can use either the numeric short codes (c-1, c-2) or the semantic codes (FY2023, BS_2023_12_31) to access context values. The semantic codes are more descriptive and self-explanatory.
